### [139] [Experimental Multiport-Network Parameter Estimation and Optimization for Multi-Bit RIS](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.02168)
*Philipp del Hougne*

Main category: physics.app-ph

TL;DR: Based on the abstract, the paper addresses the challenge of estimating MNT model parameters for wireless channels with unknown RIS design and radio environments. They propose an efficient technique combining closed-form and gradient-descent steps, validated experimentally in an 8-RIS-element setup, showing minimal performance impact despite significant model accuracy differences. Motivation: RIS-based wireless systems are rapidly advancing, but parameter estimation in unknown environments is a critical gap. Method: Combines closed-form and gradient-descent steps for parameter estimation. Result: The method effectively handles unknown environments, with minimal impact on system performance. Conclusion: The proposed technique provides a robust solution for estimating MNT model parameters, enhancing RIS performance in unknown settings.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The rapid development of RIS-based wireless systems has highlighted the need for accurate channel modeling, especially in unknown environments where traditional assumptions may not hold. This paper addresses a critical gap by providing a method to estimate model parameters without prior knowledge of the RIS design and radio environment, which is essential for practical applications. The challenge is particularly relevant as the number of RIS elements and their programmability vary, making parameter estimation complex without sufficient data.

Method: The method proposed in the paper combines closed-form solutions with gradient descent optimization. This hybrid approach efficiently handles the estimation of multiport network theory (MNT) model parameters. The technique is designed to be computationally feasible even with a higher number of parameters, leveraging the structure of the problem to iteratively refine estimates. Additionally, the method accounts for parameters that may not significantly affect performance despite being present in the model.

Result: The experimental results demonstrate that the proposed technique achieves significant parameter estimation accuracy, particularly in an environment with eight 8-bit-programmable RIS elements. The method shows robust performance even when the exact design and radio environment are unknown, leading to effective RIS configuration optimization. However, the trade-off is a slight performance loss compared to when model parameters are known a priori, indicating the robustness of the method in practical scenarios.

Conclusion: The paper concludes by highlighting the effectiveness of the proposed method in estimating MNT model parameters for unknown environments. This advancement is crucial for enabling reliable performance of RIS-based wireless systems in real-world scenarios where perfect channel knowledge is often unavailable. The method's ability to handle multi-bit programmable RIS elements and operate in unknown scattering environments makes it a valuable contribution to the field, supporting practical implementations of RIS technology without compromising performance accuracy significantly.

Abstract: Physics-consistent theoretical studies on RIS-parametrized wireless channels
use models from multiport-network theory (MNT) to capture mutual-coupling (MC)
effects. However, in practice, RIS design and radio environment are partially
or completely unknown. We fill a research gap on how to estimate the MNT model
parameters in such experimentally relevant scenarios. Our technique efficiently
combines closed-form and gradient-descent steps, and it can be applied to
multi-bit-programmable RIS elements. We discuss inevitable (but operationally
irrelevant) parameter ambiguities. We experimentally validate our technique in
an unknown rich-scattering environment parametrized by eight 8-bit-programmable
RIS elements of unknown design. We experimentally evaluate the performance of
RIS configurations optimized with the estimated MNT model and an MC-unaware
cascaded model. While the models differ in accuracy by up to 17 dB, the
end-to-end performance differences are small.

</details>


### [140] [On the Design of Corrugated Boards: A New FEM Modeling and Experimental Validation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.02189)
*Ricardo Fitas,Heinz Joachim Schaffrath,Samuel Schabel*

Main category: physics.app-ph

TL;DR: The study presents a simplified FEM approach for corrugated boards in packaging. They use homogenization and correction based on Weibull models. Results show computational efficiency and accuracy.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation:  package design optimization using FEM on corrugated boards, aiming for faster simulations without losing accuracy.

Method: Homogenization method with Weibull corrections for internal mechanisms. They transformed geometries into elastic models and used experimental data for parameter fitting.

Result: They found effective elastic properties and thickness correction using Weibull parameters, validated for accuracy.

Conclusion: Simplifies FEM modeling for efficient, accurate simulations of corrugated structures in packaging.

Abstract: This study presents a simplified FEM modeling approach suitable for large
structures made of corrugated boards, such as customized packages, based on a
homogenization method, which is combined with correction factors for internal
mechanisms. The homogenization process reduces computational time by
transforming flute geometries into equivalent elastic models. In large
deformations and in the presence of contact for a given geometry, the effective
elastic modulus in the thickness direction, as well as the effective thickness
of the structure, are corrected by two statistical Weibull distributions
representing the contact and buckling mechanisms in a corrugated board. The
Weibull parameters are obtained via experimental analysis, and such a process
is then validated. The results demonstrate that the statistical parameters
($\beta_1 = 0.14$, $\beta_2 = 1.31$) can be used for the simplistic
representation of corrugated boards, being computationally efficient. This
research contributes to the optimization of corrugated packaging design,
specifically by simplifying FEM models for faster yet equally accurate
simulations.

</details>


### [141] [Modeling the Effective Elastic Modulus and Thickness of Corrugated Boards Using Gaussian Process Regression and Expected Hypervolume Improvement](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.02208)
*Ricardo Fitas*

Main category: physics.app-ph

TL;DR: The paper presents a method combining Latin Hypercube Sampling and Gaussian Process Regression enhanced by EHVI for modeling elastic modulus and thickness of corrugated boards, achieving high accuracy with low MSE.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Evaluating mechanical properties of corrugated boards for structural optimization requires accurate modeling of their effective elastic modulus and thickness.

Method: The method uses Latin Hypercube Sampling followed by Gaussian Process Regression enhanced with Expected Hypervolume Improvement (EHVI) as a multi-objective acquisition function to model the hypersurface of Eeff and theeff.

Result: The GP model achieved an MSE of 5.24 kPa² for Eeff and 1 mm² for theeff, demonstrating high accuracy and adaptability for future applications.

Conclusion: The proposed method effectively models the mechanical properties of corrugated boards, enhancing their use in engineering applications through optimized structural design.

Abstract: This work aims to model the hypersurface of the effective elastic modulus, \(
E_{z, \text{eff}} \), and thickness, \( th_{\text{eff}} \), in corrugated
boards. A Latin Hypercube Sampling (LHS) is followed by Gaussian Process
Regression (GP), enhanced by EHVI as a multi-objective acquisition function.
Accurate modeling of \( E_{z, \text{eff}} \) and \( th_{\text{eff}} \) is
critical for optimizing the mechanical properties of corrugated materials in
engineering applications. LHS provides an efficient and straightforward
approach for an initial sampling of the input space; GP is expected to be able
to adapt to the complexity of the response surfaces by incorporating both
prediction and uncertainty. Therefore, the next points being generated and
evaluated are based on the complexity of the hypersurfaces, and some points,
especially those with higher variance, are more exploited and carry more
importance. The performance of GP with EHVI is measured by Mean Squared Error
(MSE). Prediction of GP resulted in \( \text{MSE}(E_{z, \text{eff}}) = 5.24 \,
\text{kPa}^2 \) and \( \text{MSE}(th_{\text{eff}}) = 1 \, \text{mm}^2 \). GP
possesses then improved accuracy and adaptability for future applications in
structural optimization.

</details>

Method: 直接从麦克斯韦方程推导，引入群论进行分析。

Conclusion: 方法提供了分析任意电荷电流分布下的电磁场有用工具。

Abstract: We derive an analytic solution for the electromagnetic vector potential in

### [143] [Kapitza's Pendulum as a Classical Prelude to Floquet-Magnus Theory](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.02736)
*Johannes K. Krondorfer,Maria Kainz,Matthias Diez,Andreas W. Hauser*

Main category: physics.class-ph

TL;DR: Pedagogical introduction to Floquet-Magnus theory using Kapitza's pendulum as an example. Derives equations of motion, analyzes using Floquet theory and Magnus expansion, finds analytical stability conditions. Directly applicable to quantum systems. Suitable for advanced undergrads.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper aims to introduce Floquet-Magnus theory through a well-known example to make it accessible, which is helpful for students learning the subject.

Method: They derive equations of motion for Kapitza's pendulum, apply Floquet theory and Magnus expansion to analyze the system, find analytical conditions for stabilization. The methods are foundational from classical mechanics and linear algebra. 

Result: They find analytical stability conditions and effective evolution equations, showing the techniques' applicability to quantum systems too. 

Conclusion: The paper effectively teaches the theory through a practical example, making it suitable for instruction at an undergraduate level.

Abstract: We present a pedagogical introduction to Floquet-Magnus theory through the
classical example of Kapitza's pendulum \ -- a simple system exhibiting
nontrivial dynamical stabilization under rapid periodic driving. By deriving
the equations of motion and analyzing the system via Floquet theory and the
Magnus expansion, we obtain analytical stability conditions and effective
evolution equations. While grounded in classical mechanics, the techniques are
directly applicable to periodically driven quantum systems as well. The
approach is fully analytical, using only tools from theoretical mechanics and
linear algebra, and is suitable for advanced undergraduate or graduate
students.

</details>
